Free Talk

Dismissed with a Laugh

— Seafarer

▲Daughter: Mother, will I have to marry a husband in the future?

Mother: It's up to you. But most women in the world do.

Daughter: Mother, then I'm ten years old this year. Should I go find a husband? Haven't I seen my aunt look for twenty years and still not find one?

▲Wife A: So your husband dares to deceive you?

Wife B: How can he not? Every day when he goes to the company, I always give him twenty cents for round-trip tram fare. Who knew he walked both ways but bought snacks with the money?

▲Doctor A: My consultation hours are scheduled from 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM every day.

Doctor B: So, the rest of the time, are you still studying medicine?

Doctor A: No. Collecting the consultation fees owed by the patients.

▲Son: Father, what is optimism?

Father: A person suffering from a terminal illness still hires a quack doctor to treat him. That's called optimism.

▲Customer: The parrot you sold me can't talk. I talk to it, but it never says anything.

Shopkeeper: Sir, I forgot to tell you. It really can talk, but it's deaf and can't hear you.

Strange Anecdotes of Mr. Wu Youling of Sichuan

— Fu Qinxin

Mr. Youling, named Yu, was from Chengdu, Sichuan. Hu Shi called him the old hero who single-handedly fought against the Confucian shop. This refers to Mr. Wu. He taught at Peking University for a very long time and was renowned throughout the country. I was fortunate enough to be under his wing for half a year in the Jiazi year (1924), and I know his affairs in great detail. I respectfully select those obscure and not yet widely known, and record them, to inform the scholars.

Mr. Wu lost his wife early. He had several daughters, all with extensive literary knowledge and beautiful appearance. The youngest daughter married a gentleman from Henan two years ago and is currently studying abroad with him. The second daughter fell in love with a Mr. Pan Lishan in Washington, D.C. Mr. Wu was deeply displeased that she married without informing him and ceased all communication. Mr. Wu's Beijing residence was at No. 5 Liangguo Factory. It was a secluded and comfortable place. He converted the large hall into a library, and the remaining two rooms were used as a bedroom and reception area. Only one servant was employed to provide meals and cleaning. Upon entering his hall, books and literary works lined the shelves, a dazzling array, like entering a valley of ten thousand flowers. He was often seen alone, profound and refined, as if he had found his own joy. He was truly like a person from Peach Blossom Spring.

Mr. Wu's scholarship was most beloved by the Japanese. His "Wenyu Wenlu" was practically a copy in every hand. They also extracted his speeches and reprinted them in various newspapers and magazines, such as "Sinology" and "Figures of the Dawn of China," which were the most notable. Modern Japanese writers and Sinologists with deep understanding and sympathy for Mr. Wu sent letters from overseas, expressing their warm regards. My friend Chu Yian, who was most esteemed by Mr. Wu, visited him every evening. He saw them all and spoke of them in great detail.

Yang Shukan of Sichuan, a prominent figure in the revolution, once served as Minister of Agriculture and Commerce during Duan Qirui's administration. Mr. Wu despised him. One day, they happened to meet at a friend's place. Mr. Wu remained aloof and did not offer a greeting. Afterwards, he said to others, "Mr. Yang is tempted by power and profit and has lost his footing. Not only is his personal integrity flawed, but his political life will also be ruined."

Mr. Luo Yinggong's spirit. Cheng Yuyi wept bitterly for him, even suspending performances to mourn. Mr. Wu praised him and wrote a poem to commemorate the event. I remember one of his poems: "[The orioles, parrots, silkworms, and fleas have long been a cause for sorrow. I once read of your difficulties and felt saddened by the loss of virtue. Today, I meet a national beauty in Yantai, her beauty captivating and her heart chivalrous.]" Even in occasional amusement, it was elegant and extraordinary, unlike anything ordinary.

Mr. Wu was extremely unrestrained and enjoyed frequenting brothels. His presence was often seen in the "eight districts." Every evening when the lanterns were lit and the bells jingled, there was an old man stroking his beard and smiling, reclining among the flowers, which was Mr. Wu at his happiest. His poems recording these events were fragrant and exquisite. They were once printed in a beautifully bound edition and given to friends. Even the line "[Suddenly touching my private parts, it rises like a tomb]" was included in the miscellany, which shows that he was not one to be拘泥于小节. Mr. Wu hated evil as if it were an enemy and was tired of hearing about the changes in the world. In recent years, the war has become increasingly urgent, and he knew that peace was hopeless. He decided to abandon Beijing and return to his hometown in the summer of Yichou (1925), where he secluded himself, wrote books, and enjoyed his old age. From then on, the spiritual light of Lu Dian stood alone in Chengdu.

Unbelievable Common Sense

— Yan Zhou

▲ Fish Bone Stuck in Throat: Whenever a fish bone is stuck in the throat, do not open your mouth. Take the eating utensils you are holding, such as a rice bowl or wine cup, and rotate it once to the right. Then, take a mouthful of rice or a little wine and swallow it directly into the throat. The bone will immediately be dislodged. This method was learned from the Zhuyou (incantation) department and has been tested and proven effective many times. However, the reason for it is inexplicable.

▲ Lumps on Limbs: Lumps often appear between the joints of the limbs due to careless movement. They swell larger and larger. Although not very harmful, they are unsightly. I once strained myself lifting heavy objects, and a lump rose on the back of my hand and wrist. Both Western and Chinese medicine were tried. Some said to apply a plaster, others said to cut it open, but none of it worked. Later, in Suzhou, I met a fellow townsman, Mr. Xu Guiqing, who said that rubbing it during a thunderstorm can gradually reduce it until it disappears. I tried it last summer, and it worked. Unexpectedly, it has recently reappeared, but it is very small. I plan to try it again during a thunderstorm. If anyone has the same problem, please try it for me to confirm its effectiveness.

The above two items cannot be explained scientifically, but based on my personal experience, they are unfailingly effective. Readers, please do not despise and discard them as unfounded.

New Voices for Calendar Reform

— Lü Bing

The calendar used by societies in various countries is very old. But since the European War, there have been proposals to revise it. There are several reasons, mainly that the current calendar is difficult to remember and difficult to examine. For example, the date of Easter changes every year, and the day of the week of Christmas also changes, causing great inconvenience. Recently, the Americans have revived the issue, and the voices for calendar reform are soaring. The local English evening newspaper has reported this news, but it is brief and lacks detail. According to the new calendar proposed by the Americans, each year would have 365 days, with one day removed as a public holiday at the beginning of the year, not included in the week. The remaining days would be divided equally into four seasons, each with ninety-one days. Each season would have three months, two small and one large. The small ones have thirty days, and the large ones have thirty-one days. In this way, every four years there would be a leap year, adding one day at the end of June. This so-called leap day would be a public holiday, not counted in the week, the same as the beginning of the year. In this way, leap years would not matter, and the calendar would be fixed every year. Even without using a calendar, with a little thought, one could deduce which day of the week it is. It is indeed very convenient. Recently, major cities in the United States have organized calendar reform research committees. The committee members and experts who have joined are mostly bankers, industrialists, astronomers, sociologists, and representatives of groups and governments. The European countries are also following suit. For example, the Dutch Calendar Reform Committee has recently been established, and Professor Nijland of the University of the Netherlands is personally chairing it. Mr. Nijland is a well-known astronomer and has published books on calendar reform discussions, attracting a lot of sympathy from the public. According to Western newspapers, since the Americans advocated calendar reform, countries all over the world have successively expressed their support and intend to take the same steps. As of now, there are more than ten countries, including Panama, Ecuador, Peru, Brazil, the Netherlands, France, Hungary, Cuba, and other small countries.

Overseas Tealeaves

— Tian Peng, sent from Tokyo

The vicissitudes of Wilhelm II: Wilhelm has been living a secluded and boring life since his exile in the Netherlands. Recently, he celebrated his seventy-first birthday. None of his children and grandchildren, who used to surround him, came to visit. It is said that they lacked travel expenses and could not make the trip. Wilhelm recalled the grand gatherings of the past and could not help but feel emotional.

▲ A fifteen-foot-tall stone head: The famous Italian sculptor Lamina is currently working on a stone statue of General Garibaldi, using the world's largest marble. It is said to be fifteen feet tall, and the artist standing on the shoulders only reaches his nose. It will be erected as a national landmark.

▲ A school of fish flying from the sky: A man named Karis in Rhodesia, England, suddenly saw a school of fish flying from the sky. The grounds and flower beds were covered with fish. He was shocked and nearly went mad. The citizens were also alarmed by this strange event. After careful study by interested people, it was found that the fish from a nearby pond had been swept up by a hurricane.

▲ A female poisoning gang in Hungary: A small village in Hungary called Zorno recently captured a female poisoning gang of thirty people. The investigation revealed that the women in the entire village were involved. The victims were husbands, lovers, youths, children, etc. Anyone who was disliked was poisoned to death.

▲ A car catches fire and goes to the fire department for help: In England, a steam-powered car caught fire due to negligence. The conductor panicked and did not know what to do. The police told him to quickly go to the fire department to extinguish it, and it was saved. This is a new world record for seeking help when a fire breaks out.

▲ The first trial in the Vatican: Recently, the Vatican City exercised its judicial power, which is the first case of the restoration of the Papal Court. It is a very interesting issue. There were many people in the audience. The offender was a thief. Because the laws of the Holy See have not yet been established, Italian law was temporarily cited to sentence him to three months in prison.

Red Carpet

First Performance of the Star Opera Society

— Xiu Mei

In recent years, opera clubs have sprung up on the sea, and the social elite's love of Peking Opera has been increasing day by day. Actors and employees of the Star Film Company formed the Star Opera Society four months ago. They hired famous teachers and rehearsed daily, diligently studying. Although it has not been long, the results have been remarkable. It is heard that the first dress rehearsal has been scheduled for the thirtieth of this month at the company's studio. Masterpieces from literati all around the country have been collected to be printed in a special edition paper. The performance of graceful dances and pure songs will certainly be a great event with many guests gathering. The scheduled programs are listed below. Daytime program: Tan Zhiyuan (Five Terrace Mountain), Dong Tianya, Huang Lingxuan (Exploring the Cold Kiln), Hong Zhen (Double Betrayal of the Tang), Su Wanjun, Gu Meijun (Wujia Slope), Hong Shen (Wenzhao Pass), Xu Zhiren, Tang Jie (Arresting Cao), Zheng Xiaoqiu, Gu Meijun (Meilong Town), Wang Jiting (Beaded Curtain Village), Zhou Jianyun, Hu Die (Returning to the Dragon Pavilion), Hong Shen, Zheng Zhengqiu, Xiao Ying (Yellow Crane Tower). Evening program: Zheng Shihui (Selling the Horse), Wu Jiwu (Nanyang Pass), Tang Jie (Exploring the Underworld), Wang Xianzai (Borrowing Tea), Huang Lingxuan, Huang Xuexuan (Fourth Son Visiting His Mother), Zheng Zhengqiu, Tang Jie (Golden Stage), Yan Chonglou, Zhou Jianyun (Scolding the Palace), Wang Cilong, Zhou Wenzhu (South Heavenly Gate), Zhou Jianyun, Hu Die (Joining the Army and Bidding Farewell to the Kiln), Gao Zhanfei, Dong Tianya (Beheading the Son at the Gate).

The Theatrical Skills of Kunqu Actress Jing Yanfang

— Shu Lin

Kunqu actress Jing Yanfang is the beloved daughter of Jing Yufeng. She is twenty-seven years old and has a slender figure. She has been learning Qingyi and Huashan plays from her mother for many years. She is intelligent and diligent and has mastered more than thirty plays. She is currently performing at the Great World (amusement park) with the Da Jing class (opera troupe). I do not usually praise Kunqu actresses. Yesterday, at the insistence of a friend, I happened to pass by and saw Yanfang performing "Scolding the Palace." I could not help but stop and listen. The Yaoban (clapper aria) in the first scene and the Daoban (reversed aria), Huilong tune, and slow Sanzheizi (three-beat rhythm) in the second scene were all smooth and natural. The Kuai Sanzheizi in the latter two halls were also fluent and pleasant to hear. Although this play does not have much physical acting, listening to these few sections of singing is like tasting a small piece of the whole tripod, which is enough to know its general features. According to my friend, her other plays, such as the flexibility of her drunken waist work, the charm of her performance, and the heavy singing in "Yu Tang Chun," all show her strengths. There are also plays such as "Magu's Birthday Celebration," "Mantou Temple," "Flying to the Moon," and "Scattering Flowers." Every time she appears on stage, the embroidered curtain is lifted, and the applause is like thunder. It can be seen that Yanfang's theatrical skills certainly have the ability to attract audiences.

Warmth in My Heart (155)

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 10: Flaming Inferno, Grandstand Admiring a Filial Daughter, Red Carpet Laid Out, Improvised Meeting with Famous Actors. That Zhang's Weichun Garden is also someone's garden. That garden owner, Mr. Zhang, is from Changzhou. He served several terms as Daotai in the Qing Dynasty. The most mysterious kind of bureaucrat was called Daotai. The most omnipotent kind of official was also Daotai. In the past, in Nanjing alone, there were several hundred candidates for Daotai. Therefore, some people also said that Nanjing had three many: many kidnappers, many donkeys, many candidates for Daotai. Being a Daotai could be good or bad. Those who got rich and important positions were Red Daotai. Even the Fan-Tai (provincial treasurer) and Nie-Tai (provincial judge) could not compare with him. They could plunder hundreds of thousands of silver in a year and leave. The black ones were completely blackened. They could be candidates for more than ten years and not get any assignments, ending up eating their fill and running out of money, not even having enough robes to go to the yamen. There were also some like that. Moreover, Daotais had all kinds of abilities and could be any kind of official. Civilian ones could be school Daotai or grain Daotai. Military ones could be military preparation Daotai. Speaking of foreign affairs assignments, they were also Daotai. That garden owner, Mr. Zhang, was also a Daotai. With the gains from his official career, he came to Shanghai and built this garden. Some people said that he was impeached by his superiors and returned home as a corrupt official. That is not our concern. In short, he was willing to make this private garden public. Coming to his garden did not require buying a ticket. Anyone could run in. This had a bit of an egalitarian flavor. He had a large foreign-style building. Rather than saying it was a garden, it was more like a hall for gatherings. Sitting in that foreign-style building required ordering a bowl of tea. The waiter would immediately bring up several dishes: melon seeds, peanuts, and candy. You could eat as much as you wanted. Each bowl of tea cost two jiao, and each dish cost only five fen. Considering the cost of living at that time, it was not expensive at all. At that time, some people who were someone's friends would rather stroll around the periphery of the foreign-style building than dare to go inside. When the garden owner encountered festivals or the New Year holidays or the race season, he would supervise the tea servers and waiters in the foreign-style building, checking how many tables were serving tea and how much tea they could sell. When there were many visitors, they could sell hundreds of bowls of tea a day. This could be considered a source of income for the garden owner. Moreover, he was always smiling. He seemed to recognize everyone, as if he were a receptionist there. When he met acquaintances, he would sit at this table and then at that table, chatting all the way. Especially the courtesans in the hall, especially the older ones, he would recognize even more. He would definitely come over and exchange a few words with them. They would naturally call him "Master Zhang" and chat with him. In addition, he would lend this foreign-style building to people for meetings. Any large meeting would be held at Zhang Garden. Any exciting ____ would be held at Zhang Garden. Because, in Shanghai, apart from this Zhang Garden, there was no place that was so versatile and suitable for combining styles.

Yarn Prices Recently Fell Nearly Fifty Taels

▲ Thick Accumulation of Inventory...Sluggish Actual Demand

▲ Chaotic Situation...Strong Selling Pressure

The yarn market trend is quite weak, due to the increasing inventory and the stagnation in sales of 10-count coarse yarn and a batch of unsold goods on the market. Therefore, although buyers are trying their best, they ultimately cannot support it. In addition, the chaotic situation shows signs of prolonging. As a result, sellers are becoming more courageous and exerting more pressure. Therefore, the yarn price, which has been brewing for a long time this month, is now approaching the end of the month. Buyers see the overall situation as unfavorable and have no intention of taking delivery, resulting in a very poor situation. The 50 tael threshold is difficult to maintain, and most targets must be 46-47 taels, but some are not giving up on the idea of going long because of the cheap base.

▲ This Month's Yarn Sellers Prepared to Deliver, Suffered a Sharp Drop of Two Jiao Six Fen, First Bid Auction, Market Opening. Grain and Rice Market Sales Brisk and Prices Rise

▲ Top White Japonica Reaches 20 Yuan and 5 Jiao...Food for the People Deserves Attention ▲ Zhabei, Yesterday the market rose again, with very few ships coming from the interior. The market in this street is brisk. Top-quality Northern Japonica rice is very scarce, so the price reached 20 yuan and 5 jiao. Ordinary Middle Grade rice generally increased by several jiao. Currently, river inventory is gradually thinning. The prices in the producing and selling areas are not economical. At this time of year, when the new harvest is not yet available, the food supply in Shanghai in the future is a matter of great concern. Local sales are mainly Japonica rice, so new high prices are appearing. Thin Indica rice has attracted interest from customer merchants, and the trend is active. Both buyers and sellers are shouting for tightness. Sheep Du Xian rice has risen by one or two jiao due to the sharp rise in foreign rice. Customer ports also have strong demand for Indica rice, but retail sales are not smooth, and prices are following the general trend. Buying interest in White Yuan rice is still flat, and various firms are not eager to purchase, so there is no significant increase or decrease.

▲ Shanghai South, Ships arriving from the river are not strong, and sales were very sluggish in the early morning, but then improved due to tight news from Zhabei. Changzhou, Wuxi, Suzhou, and other Japonica rice prices were initially flat but then became firm, with about one jiao difference. Villagers and customers are waiting and watching due to the current high prices, but sellers, on the other hand, are raising prices due to the strong market in the interior. There are also rumors that a certain customer merchant is purchasing and hoarding goods extensively in the interior. Although this is just hearsay, it is not without reason, so the goals of buyers and sellers are even more firm. Sales of Southern Shanghai's thin early rice are relatively weak, and incoming goods are not abundant, but the market price is not easy to rise again. Sheep Du Xian rice is actually very scarce here. Although a few shipments have arrived, foreign rice prices are not rising, and therefore the price of this rice is also increasing. The sales are also brisk. The changes are similar to those in the North Market, and the price of hanging embryos is slightly moving, and the market is neither good nor bad.

Local News

Owner of American Sun Newspaper Flew to Shanghai Yesterday

▲ Departed from London on February 11

▲ Flew Across the Three Continents of Europe, Africa, and Asia to Arrive

▲ Currently Deciding to Continue Flying to Korea and Japan

Mr. White Locke, the owner of the American Baltimore Sun, prepared a large monoplane and departed from London on February 11, flying across the three continents of Europe, Africa, and Asia. Yesterday morning at 7 o'clock, he continued flying to Shanghai from Hong Kong, and flew to Hongqiao Airport at 3:45 in the afternoon, landing safely. White Locke is currently staying at the Dahua Hotel. It is reported that he has decided to continue flying to Seoul in Korea and Tokyo in Japan, but the date of departure from Shanghai has not yet been determined.

▲ Safely Arrived in Shanghai. Local Chinese and foreign dignitaries concerned received the confirmation that White Locke continued to fly to Shanghai from Hong Kong, and dozens of people went to Hongqiao Airport yesterday afternoon to welcome him. They waited until 3:30, and heard the rumbling of the airplane engine in the air, and looked up to see a silver airplane flying from the east. Bai Locke and his airplane, photographed by Huifang Photography Studio at the Racecourse

The people standing at the airport to welcome him immediately waved their handkerchiefs to signal, and the airplane circled the field twice and landed leisurely. It was 3:45. The welcomers surrounded the fuselage, and White Locke, his secretary, and the pilot came out and shook hands and talked with the welcomers. Then they drove to the Dahua Hotel to stay.

▲ A Glimpse of the Fuselage. The airplane that White Locke was riding in was named [Maryland Liberty State] and was a huge monoplane. The fuselage was three colors, the head was silver-white, the middle section was black, and the tail was cyan-blue. The wings were golden yellow. The interior of the airplane had five seats and was quite comfortable. It was equipped with three engines, which were started at the same time when flying. The fuselage weighed 700 pounds, carried 500 pounds, and had 300 horsepower. It could fly continuously in the air for 12 hours. The average speed was 120 miles per hour. It was made in the Netherlands.

▲ White Locke's Remarks. White Locke, the owner of the Sun Newspaper, has been engaged in the news business for 14 years. The Baltimore Sun, which he runs, is divided into morning and evening editions. White Locke told this newspaper's reporter at the Dahua Hotel yesterday, "I (White Locke referred to himself below) took off from London on February 11 and first landed in Marseille, France. Then I continued to fly through 13 cities including Cairo, Beckett, Bangok, and Hanoi, and arrived in Hong Kong last Wednesday. After arriving in Shanghai today, there is no definite date for departure. I will not fly to Nanjing and Beiping, but China Airlines has invited me to take the company's Shanghai-Hankou airplane for a trip to Beijing and Hankou, but it has not yet been determined. After that, I decided to fly to Seoul in Korea and then to Tokyo in Japan, and then take a boat back to the United States. My flight has been very smooth along the way. It was quite interesting to see the Siamese people performing Chinese martial arts in Bangok. The purpose of my trip is purely commercial and experimental, and to use the speed of flight to travel the world, and to prove that airplanes have a close relationship with the news business. When we flew to a part of Africa, there were more than a dozen British people who had no newspapers to read and had not received letters for several weeks. When we flew to that place and showed them the newspapers we were carrying, the British people there competed to read them. A newspaper was as precious as a treasure and worth a lot of money. From Hong Kong to Shanghai, it only takes one day, which is very convenient for the transmission of newspapers and communications."

Wang Zhengting Reports on Recent Diplomatic Matters

▲ Russia Requests Expansion of Conference Scope

▲ Foreign Ministry Has Telegraphed Liaoning to Inquire About Everything

Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting reported to newspaper reporters yesterday on recent diplomatic news. They are described separately below:

▲ Recovery of French Concession Police Station. Foreign Minister Wang said that regarding the recovery of the French Concession Police Station in Shanghai, the Foreign Ministry sent a note to the French Minister, requesting that he send personnel to Beijing as soon as possible to discuss reorganization methods. However, since the note was issued, the French side has not made any response. It is thought that because the French cabinet has changed repeatedly, the China issue has been put on hold. As for the outside rumors that the Foreign Ministry will directly send the note to Paris because the French Minister is about to return home, this is the statement of someone who does not understand diplomatic procedures, because even if the French Minister leaves, there must be a chargé d'affaires to exercise the powers of the Minister, and there is no reason to send it directly to Paris.

▲ Shanghai Provisional Court. The reorganization of the Provisional Court of the Public Concession is scheduled to be implemented on April 1 and will not be postponed. The reorganization plan is entirely based on the agreement signed in Beijing by the representatives of various countries. Xu Mo, Director of the European and American Department, came to Shanghai a few days ago to make further contacts with the representatives of various countries, and the result was very satisfactory, and the reorganization can be carried out smoothly.

▲ Weihaiwei Issue. Regarding the recovery of the Weihaiwei issue, an agreement has been largely reached. When British Minister Lampson arrives in Beijing at the end of this month, it can be formally signed after a brief discussion.

▲ Sino-Russian Conference Period. The official Sino-Russian conference is scheduled to be held in mid-next month. Our representative, Mo Dehui, is scheduled to depart for Moscow on April 10. The news reported by Japan stated that Russia refused to open peace talks and refused our representative, and also said that Russia requested to expand the scope of the conference, otherwise it would send troops to disturb the border. The Foreign Ministry has not received an official report and has telegraphed Liaoning to inquire about everything, but there is no reply yet.

Sino-Japanese Negotiations Underway

Foreign Minister Wang Met With Shigemitsu Yesterday

▲ Exchanged Views on Legal Rights Issues

▲ Shigemitsu Will Go to Beijing to Continue Negotiations

Regarding the legal jurisdiction issue in the Sino-Japanese Treaty of Commerce, Japanese Chargé d'Affaires Shigemitsu Kui has repeatedly made informal contacts with Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting. Yesterday afternoon at approximately 3 o'clock, Wang Zhengting met with Shigemitsu at the Diplomatic Discussion Association on Avenue Joffre and talked for about an hour before Shigemitsu took his leave. The content was still discussing the legal rights issue, and the opinions of both sides are becoming closer. The date of resolution should not be far away. Foreign Minister Wang told this newspaper's reporter yesterday that the most important parts of the Sino-Japanese Treaty of Commerce are tariff jurisdiction and inland navigation rights. Since the tariff issue has been resolved, we are now negotiating the legal jurisdiction issue. Today's meeting was to exchange informal views on this issue. When opinions gradually become consistent, a formal meeting will be held to sign a draft. I will return to Beijing tonight (that is, last night), and Shigemitsu will go to Beijing tomorrow night (that is, tonight) to continue negotiations. There are rumors that the Japanese government will appoint Hirota as the ambassador to China to be responsible for Sino-Japanese negotiations, but Shigemitsu never mentioned it, and the Foreign Ministry has not received any reports, so I am afraid it is not true.

Yesterday's Mediation Decision on Pharmaceutical Industry Dispute

▲ 128 Workers to Resume Work Today

▲ 51 Unqualified Workers to be Laid Off

The labor-management dispute in the city's pharmaceutical industry over the hiring of unemployed workers had reached extreme positions on both sides, leading to work slowdowns and market shutdowns. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, along with the Municipal Party Headquarters and Public Security Bureau, appointed representatives to form a mediation committee, repeatedly convening both parties for mediation. Yesterday, the Pharmaceutical Association once again petitioned the Bureau of Social Affairs to conduct mediation and make a swift decision, stating that it was no longer appropriate to prolong the situation, as it was affecting patients. Yesterday, the mediation committee made a fair decision, ordering the industry's labor and management groups to comply and not to engage in further work slowdowns or market shutdowns. The decision of the case mediation is found below, in its original text:

▲ Decision of the Shanghai Special Municipality Labor-Management Dispute Mediation Committee (Mediation No. 400) Disputing Parties: Labor: Pharmaceutical Workers Union; Management: Preparatory Committee of the Pharmaceutical Industry Association (formerly the Pharmaceutical Division of the Business and People's Association). The above-mentioned disputing parties, due to the labor side's demand for the management side to hire unemployed workers, resulting in a strike dispute, which was mediated by the committee. [Reason] The Pharmaceutical Workers Union, due to the busyness of employed workers who suffer from mental stress, and the difficult lives of unemployed workers who suffer from economic oppression, proposed relief measures and petitioned the Bureau of Social Affairs and the Municipal Party Headquarters to order the management to hire more workers to accommodate unemployed workers. The Bureau of Social Affairs ordered the unemployed workers in the industry to register first, and then together with the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Civil Training Committee,

Page 14

drafted eight review standards to examine the qualifications of the registered unemployed workers. The initial review resulted in 67 people being deemed qualified, 64 people requiring investigation, and 51 people being unqualified. The Civil Training Committee and the Bureau of Social Affairs then jointly dispatched people to conduct a thorough investigation of those who required investigation, and most of them were also found to be qualified. Later, after an inspection by the Municipal Party Chief for a period of time, it was also discovered that among the 67 people who had passed the review, Han Zuxin and Chen Yongxian were key members of the Pharmaceutical Workers Mutual Aid Society organized by the Communist Party, and Qin Falong, Qiu Zijiang, Qiu Rongchun, Zhong Zhifang, Xu Fukang, Feng Junda, Ye Qixiang, Yang Guangcai, and Zhang Huaqing, a total of nine people, had changed to other occupations and would not be given relief. Instead, 11 people who had not registered, including Zhou Yaseng, Sun Kaide, Chen Shanzhang, Qiu Wangzhou, Guo Yuankang, Kong Kailin, Ying Denghua, Li Huaifang, Liu Shuiliang, Chen Fanglin, and Gu Mingsheng, were added. In total, 131 unemployed workers were deemed qualified according to the review standards. Except for the two people already hired by Jiang Yanze for recording purposes and one person hired by Zhou Baifu, there are still 128 people who should be given relief. The Bureau of Social Affairs and the Civil Training Committee repeatedly sent people to secretly investigate the business situation of various pharmaceutical stores and the economic conditions of unemployed pharmaceutical workers. They learned that each prescription at Hu Qing Yu Tang, Tong Han Chun, Cai Tongde, and other pharmacies took more than four hours to be filled. Smaller stores such as Wang Daji, Ye Tiande, and Xi Liangji also took two to three hours to fill each prescription. If it was a chronic illness, it wouldn't matter, but in the case of an acute illness, such as meningitis, how could the patient wait for four hours or two to three hours? The so-called "medicine cures the illness" was almost becoming an empty phrase. Moreover, each prescription took four hours to fill, so the busyness of the workers can be imagined. Due to the busyness, mistakes were inevitable, and it was difficult to avoid mistakes in the medicine, which harmed people's lives. As a result, there were frequent cases of patients negotiating with stores due to errors in the medicine. Therefore, based on the principle that medicine is used to treat illnesses, all pharmacies with thriving businesses should consider the circumstances and hire more staff to avoid harming patients and to reduce the mental stress on existing workers. The fact that current employees were willing to strike to demand that stores hire unemployed workers was likely motivated by this. When the committee convened for mediation, the management representatives stated that since the government had issued an order for the management to give priority to hiring, the management naturally could not accept the placement. However, the meaning of the four words "give priority to hiring" means that when the management has the need to hire employees for business reasons, they should give priority to hiring the unemployed workers. The intention is very clear. If, as the management claimed, they only needed to wait until a store fired someone and then choose one of the unemployed workers to fill the vacancy in order to be considered as complying with the "give priority to hiring" requirement, then would it be possible to ask whether all pharmacies in the city would never hire employees again regardless of the business situation, and whether newly opened pharmacies could not hire employees? According to common sense, this is not reasonable. Therefore, what needs to be resolved now is whether, based on the current business situation of the pharmacies, there is still no need to hire more employees. The pharmaceutical industry management, regardless of its business situation, only knew to call for rejection of the placement, and did not mention whether there was a need to hire more employees, and even refused the Party Headquarters' call for consultation, which aroused the strike and caused great losses, which is very regrettable. The committee believes that at a time when epidemics are rampant, the strike trend cannot be allowed to continue. The original employees should resume work uniformly at 9:00 AM on March 25th, with wages paid as usual for the strike period. Although the operating surpluses of 53 pharmacies, including Hu Qing Yu Tang, varied last year, their thriving businesses and the busyness of their employees were similar. For the sake of social welfare, it is believed that they all have the need to hire more workers. The 128 unemployed workers, including Zheng Xizhou, who have been examined and qualified by the Civil Training Committee and the Bureau of Social Affairs, should be ordered to be hired separately by the respective stores. These newly hired employees must also report to work uniformly at 9:00 AM on the 25th. This will enable prescriptions to be filled more quickly than before, reducing losses for patients, and slightly relieving the economic oppression of unemployed workers. The committee believes that this approach not only coincides with the principles of developing industry and supporting labor, but also contributes to social security. Based on the above reasons, with the consent and signatures of the majority of the committee members, a decision is hereby made as the main text. Chairman of the Committee Guo Yongxi (seal), Committee Member Hou Dachun (signature), Committee Member Zhang Shouchun (seal), Committee Member Zhao Zhenhui (signature), Committee Member Fang Qingjian (signature), Committee Member Zhuang Meitang, Committee Member Zhang Zhihao, Recorder Wang Zhiqin, Ordered on March 24th of the 19th year of the Republic of China.

Wu Yourong Seeks Liberation for Overseas Chinese in Taiwan

▲ Letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs: Wu Yourong, representative of the overseas Chinese on the whole island of Taiwan, received a letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs stating that it was directly replying to the letter from Ye Yunxiang and others regarding the exaction of fees by the passport-issuing authorities for overseas Chinese going to Taiwan, and requesting that it be forwarded to the Fujian Provincial Government. The Ministry has recently formulated interim measures for the issuance of passports, which are universally implemented by all passport-issuing authorities. These authorities should charge fees in accordance with the regulations and should not make any further demands. According to these measures, workers are treated very favorably and are charged only half the fee. Overseas Chinese going to Taiwan should also weigh the advantages and disadvantages and should no longer obtain passports from the Nankoku Company, which would only be self-humiliating. In addition to informing the Fujian Provincial Government to take concrete action, it is hereby informed for your reference and to inform Ye Yunxiang and others to instruct the overseas Chinese going to Taiwan to be sure to apply for passports in accordance with the regulations in the future. To Wu Yourong, representative of the overseas Chinese on the whole island of Taiwan, from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

▲ Representative's Suggestion: Wu Yourong, representative of the overseas Chinese on the whole island of Taiwan, telegraphed the Taiwan Chinese General Association stating, to all executive committee members of the Taiwan Chinese General Association and all executive committee members of all Taiwan associations, and to all overseas Chinese, may the above information be known. The previous letter requested that the reply letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs be forwarded to all overseas Chinese to apply for passports in accordance with the regulations in the future and to no longer obtain passports from the Nankoku Company, which would only be self-humiliating. It is hoped that you have received and transmitted the instructions. Regarding the establishment of a consulate, I have repeatedly urged the Central National Government and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and it is now under negotiation and will be realized soon. As for the educational affairs of the Taiwanese overseas Chinese, I have repeatedly stated to the Ministry of Education the various forms of oppression by the Taiwanese government and asked for instructions. Today's newspaper reports that the Ministry of Education consulted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the 20th, requesting that the Japanese government be negotiated not to interfere with the education of the Taiwanese overseas Chinese. It can be seen that the government cares for the Taiwanese overseas Chinese in every possible way. I am very pleased to hear this news. I hope that the General Association and local associations will actively carry out education for the overseas Chinese and select outstanding children to come to the country to study in order to achieve great achievements. I have found that the Taiwanese government has always had various unequal and harsh laws in its treatment of overseas Chinese, which is completely different from its treatment of other foreigners. Now that the abolition and revision of the Sino-Japanese treaty are in preparation, I believe that my General Association should extract these harsh laws that abuse overseas Chinese one by one, add explanations, and draft a detailed petition to be sent to Shanghai, so that it can be presented to the Central National Government and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in person. When negotiations begin in the future, they can be handled together to avoid the trouble of separate negotiations in the future. Also, I believe that my Taiwanese overseas Chinese have few communication channels in the country and are very isolated in everything. Although I have tried my best to promote and publicize in recent years, my personal talent and ability are limited, and due to economic oppression, I have not been able to travel back and forth between China and Taiwan frequently to discuss everything in person, which has hindered progress. I believe that each association on the island should bear the expenses on a monthly basis and select a number of cadres to work between Nanjing and Shanghai to engage in liaison, publicity, guidance, and reception work. This would be of some help to the future of the liberation of the Taiwanese overseas Chinese. My humble opinion, is it appropriate, please make a public decision. Wu Yourong (seal).

Report on Relief Work in Eastern Zhejiang by the Joint Chinese and Foreign Relief Committee

The Shanghai Joint Chinese and Foreign Relief Committee received a telegram yesterday from the Linhai Relief Office stating that after investigation, the disaster in Linhai County is widespread and severe, with approximately 80,000 people in dire need of relief to survive. Among them, about 50,000 to 60,000 people are in the coastal disaster areas. In addition to the winter relief already distributed, there are about 20,000 to 30,000 people in the urban area and various townships who have not yet received assistance due to insufficient funds. The office has held meetings and decided to distribute aid one by one. The situation of borrowing silver dollars for distribution in the urban area was previously reported by telegram. Upon receiving 5,000 silver dollars, the investigators were urged to complete their investigations in various townships by February 28th, and distribution stations were set up in different districts for supervised distribution. According to reports from the relief workers, from February 28th to March 8th, disaster victims with tickets came to the stations to receive relief, and the amounts were disbursed accordingly. In this statistic, a total of 8,000 "fairness" relief tickets were issued, and more than 4,700 silver dollars were distributed. Expenses for investigation travel and station supplies totaled about 200 dollars. A detailed report will be submitted after all relief tickets are collected. The disaster situation in Linhai County is the most severe in all of Zhejiang. With spring plowing approaching, seeds are completely lacking, and countless hungry people are fleeing. Once they return, they will have no capital for cultivation, and their livelihoods will be cut off, inevitably endangering public order, with significant repercussions. Therefore, it is earnestly requested that an additional 20,000 dollars be allocated for spring relief to enable the disaster victims to live and prevent the loss of the spring planting season. We respectfully request approval and implementation, awaiting orders with utmost urgency. Hou Changling, Chief Director, and Wen Lesheng, Deputy Director, Shanghai Joint Chinese and Foreign Relief Committee, Linhai Relief Office, bow in cold weather.

Baoying County Executive Committee Comes to Shanghai to Beg for Relief

▲ A Detailed Account of the Disaster Situation in the Past Two Years

Baoying County has experienced two years of famine, with an extraordinarily severe disaster situation, unprecedented among the counties of Jiangsu Province. In the countryside, most of the disaster victims are filling their stomachs with grass roots and tree bark, resulting in the death of many young and strong people. The County Executive Committee resolved to send Committee Member Hu Yuzhang to Shanghai to appeal to all parties. Mr. Hu arrived in Shanghai yesterday and is staying at the New Huizhong Hostel on Sanma Road. The letter from the County Executive Committee to the Jiangsu Provincial Temporary Relief Committee is recorded below: To begin, our county has suffered from consecutive years of famine, especially last autumn. In the eastern townships, nine out of ten households are empty. Strong young men are scattered in all directions, displaced and destitute. The elderly, weak, women, and children are unable to move or beg for food, and are forced to fill their stomachs with grass roots and tree bark. Their faces are swollen, and countless numbers are filling ditches. In this period between harvests, the situation is deteriorating daily. Although charitable individuals from various parties have provided relief funds, it is like a drop in the bucket and cannot provide even a fraction of the necessary aid. We have long admired your committee's spirit of universal love, and earnestly request that you generously provide relief and swift assistance. On behalf of the disaster victims, we bow our heads nine times in supplication. In addition to resolving to send Committee Member Yuzhang to your committee to personally explain everything, we are sending this letter to request your attention and assistance.

Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities Exempts All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association from Taxes on Domestic Goods Advertisements

▲ Handling Fees Charged According to Regulations

The All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association in Shanghai, in order to solicit supplies and promote domestic goods, jointly organized a temporary domestic goods market at the Penglai Market with domestic goods groups. They printed large, low-price advertisements and requested the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities to exempt them from advertising taxes. The bureau, considering its charitable nature, replied that it would completely exempt the advertising tax, but would charge handling fees according to regulations to subsidize government registration and stamping costs. Regarding the association's complaint in the letter that the Shanghai South Advertisement Management Office was creating difficulties for domestic goods advertisements, it also attached a statement. The original letter is as follows: In reply to your letter of March 17th, along with the attached advertisement sample, we acknowledge receipt. Although the central government has issued an order to exempt domestic goods advertisements from taxes, it stipulates that luxury goods and entertainment products should still be taxed according to regulations. The goods listed in your market still include a portion of luxury goods and entertainment products, so the advertisements cannot be completely exempted from taxes. Moreover, the matter of exempting domestic goods advertisements in this city is still under discussion and is being referred to the municipal government for instructions. However, since your market is established to save disaster victims, which is a charitable endeavor, the advertising tax can be completely exempted. As for handling fees, according to Article 16 of the city's Advertising Management Regulations, all tax-exempt advertisements must pay handling fees. The purpose of this fee is to subsidize government registration and stamping costs, so the amount is very small and does not impose a significant burden on merchants. Furthermore, regarding your letter's indication that our bureau's Advertising Management Office is creating difficulties for your market's advertisements, we have found that the office can only enforce the regulations when stamping and purchasing, and has no authority to change or obstruct matters. There may be a misunderstanding. Therefore, we are responding to the above and hope that you will continue to handle matters in accordance with the regulations. This is addressed to the All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association Temporary Domestic Goods Market Committee.

Red Wood Workers Demand Wage Increase

The red wood workers of this city convened all the workers yesterday to discuss wage increase methods. After investigating the wages of various groups of workers, the workers reported the wage situation of each group. The workers believed that the wages of various groups have increased in recent years, but only their group has not received a wage increase. Last year, they requested this from the shop owners, but they used the excuse of slow business to dodge and evade the issue. After investigating, all the workshops are now hiring additional workers, and the business is not bad, so wages should be increased immediately. Moreover, the wages they set are the lowest. Most wages are calculated by piecework, and only a few are paid monthly. After discussion, it was decided that the wage level should be the same as other groups. They are now printing leaflets listing the wages set by other groups and distributing them to the shop owners, and will demand a wage increase, with a deadline of five days for a response. Representatives will also be sent to the shop owners to explain everything and request prompt approval to ensure peace of mind at work.

Case of Death in a Hotel

▲ Guo Jinhua and Lu Fengzhi

▲ Love Suddenly Encounters Obstacles

▲ Hand in Hand, They Seek Death in a Hotel

▲ Guo is Dead, Lu Can Still be Saved

Guo Jinhua, a 25-year-old man from Zhongshan, Guangdong, checked into Room 447 of a large hotel on Nanjing Road the afternoon before yesterday with his lover. Guo was dressed in Western clothes and was very handsome, while the woman, claiming to be surnamed Tang, had short hair, leather shoes, and fashionable clothes. Guo registered on the guest register under the alias Huang Zhihua. The tea boy, seeing their lavish behavior, assumed they were from a wealthy family and did not pay much attention to them. Guo and his girlfriend went out again at 9:00 p.m. the night before and came back with many kinds of fruits, laughing as usual. Then, they closed the door and tried to go to sleep. At about 9:00 a.m. yesterday morning, the tea boy and others heard the sound of vomiting from Room 447. Realizing that something might be wrong, they pounded on the door, but there was no response. The tea boy reported to the cashier, who climbed into the room through the transom above the door. He saw that the man's face was pale and his breath had stopped, while the woman was also dying and could still be saved. The hotel staff then reported to the Lao Zha police station. After receiving the news, the police chief immediately ordered Chinese detectives to investigate. They found a Lysol bottle on the table, indicating a severe overdose. Several business cards were found on his body, signed Guo Jinhua. Only then did they realize that Huang Zhihua on the guest register was not his real name. The body was then sent to the forensic examination office on Feilun Road. Since the woman was still breathing, the detectives immediately sent a patrolman to accompany her to the Guangren Hospital for treatment. After several injections of life-saving drugs by the doctor, she slightly regained consciousness. She said her name was Lu Fengzhi, also from Guangdong. This suicide was due to obstacles in love, which prevented a satisfactory outcome, so they resorted to this strategy.

Petitioning Group of Monks from the Shousheng Temple

▲ Shousheng Temple is Limited to Move Today

▲ More than One Hundred Monks are Greatly Alarmed

▲ Marching in Formation with Incense to Petition

▲ A Strange Sight at the Provisional Court Yesterday

The Shousheng Temple on Beijing Road and the Huzhou Society organized by Huzhou people in Shanghai are involved in a lawsuit in the Provisional Court over the temple's land for many years. The Huzhou Society wanted to rebuild the temple into the Ying Shi (ie, Chen Qimei, the former Shanghai military governor) Memorial Hall. The Provisional Court has ruled that the abbot of the temple, Di Ming, etc., should move out. Di Ming refused to accept and filed an appeal. The Court of Appeal again posted a notice on the 15th of this month rejecting the appeal of the monks Di Ming, etc., against the decision to move out, and the appellant was responsible for the appeal costs. The court issued an order on the 19th, setting a deadline of the 25th of this month for the move. After receiving the order, the monks of the temple were greatly alarmed, and the abbot Di Ming was especially anxious. They believed that once they moved, more than one hundred monks would lose their place to live, and the pain of being displaced would be deeply felt. They once gathered all the monks in the temple to discuss ways to try to save the situation. As a result, they decided that all the monks in the temple would hold incense and go to the Provisional Court to petition. The petition banners were prepared the day before yesterday. The banners were made of white paper, rectangular in shape, with the four characters [Huzhou Fellow Townsmen] written horizontally at the top, and then the following written vertically: [Do not speak of justice. Confiscate temple property.], [Do not speak of humanity. Confiscate Shousheng],

[Private property of the temple.], [Powerful forces. Monks have no resistance.]. The lines were divided into two or three lines. Until ten o'clock yesterday morning, the petitioning group elected three monks, Di Ming, Mao Lin, and Fa Cheng, as leaders. Each held a lit incense stick in their right hand and a banner in their left hand. They departed from the Shousheng Temple in formation, followed Zhejiang Road, passed the old Garbage Bridge, and went straight to the Provisional Court, lining up on the pavement inside the gate. This monk petitioning group was still a first in the concession. Therefore, the viewers stood around like a wall in an instant. These one hundred and several dozen monks also complained to everyone they met. Then, the three leaders, Di Ming, etc., went up to the second floor to visit the president to hand over the petition in person, requesting a solution to the housing problem. The doorman informed them that President Xu was not in the court at the moment. Therefore, the three monks went back downstairs and talked with their companions. Some advocated waiting for the president to come to the court before submitting the request again. Later, the court instructed the three monks, Di Ming, Mao Lin, and Fa Cheng, to temporarily rest in the rest room behind the first courtroom. At around eleven o'clock, they had still not met the president. The three leaders then followed the instructions of a certain clerk who was responsible for the reception and sent the petition held by Mao Lin to the receiving and dispatch office, requesting that it be forwarded. After the receiving and dispatch office gave a receipt, they left with the two monks, Di Ming and Fa Cheng, to the pavement, explained the situation, and still led the monks, holding incense and banners, back to the temple in an orderly manner to await a solution.

Monk of Wanfu Temple Extorted

▲ Monks Make Things Difficult for Monks

▲ Negotiations Open at the Juelu Hotel

▲ Three Hundred Dollars Not Lost

▲ Extortion Crime Imprisonment for Two Months

The monk Jie Chan, whose registered residence is in Dongtai, is a 35-year-old abbot of the Wanfu Temples in southern Chengdu for many years. The temple is very popular, and there are many who covet it. At 7:30 a.m. the day before yesterday, Dao Feng, the former abbot of the Taiping Temple (surname Shen, from Hefei, 59 years old), and two men in short clothes, A and B, arrived by car at the Wanfu Temple. A got out of the car first and invited Jie Chan out to talk. He was lured into the car and driven to the entrance of the Jue Lu Hotel on Xizang Road. They got out of the car together and entered Room 56 of the hotel. Using intimidating tactics, they demanded a thousand gold coins. Jie Chan, being in their sphere of influence, agreed to give a hundred gold coins. Then one side backed down, and the other side increased the demand. At that time, they negotiated three hundred dollars. The abbot Jie Chan wrote two IOUs, one for two hundred dollars and one for one hundred dollars, to Dao Feng, and then was allowed to regain his freedom. After Jie Chan left the hotel, he felt that remaining silent would not prevent future troubles. He reported to the Xinzha Police Station. The police chief sent detective Zhang Ankang and Western detectives to investigate and found that Dao Feng was hiding at 372 Yunhua Lane, Caishi Road in the French Concession. They went to arrest Dao Feng together with the French police and searched and found the two IOUs written by Jie Chan. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Provisional Court, where Luo, the judge, conducted the trial. Jie Chan stated the situation of the defendant colluding with others to extort money. Later, the waiter of the Jue Lu Hotel was also summoned to testify, saying that the defendant had come to open Room 56 at the time, claiming to be surnamed Zhang. Zhu Genrong, a temple helper from Wanfu Temple, testified that the defendant and two men in short clothes came to invite the abbot out the morning before, and when I heard the news and chased out of the temple, the defendant and others had already driven the abbot away in a car. The car number was not identified. When asked about Dao Feng's confession, he said that he had a good impression of Jie Chan. In June of the previous year, when I was the abbot of Taiping Temple, the plaintiff boarded in my temple. Because he was economically strapped, I lent him two hundred dollars. Later, the Taiping Temple was closed by the authorities. In April of last year, I boarded at the Wanfu Temple, which the plaintiff was abbot of, and was borrowed another one hundred dollars. Neither of the two loans were documented. Recently, I heard that Jie Chan did not abide by the precepts, took a wife and concubines, and was addicted to opium. He set up a brothel, but the loans had not been repaid. Therefore, I went to the temple the day before yesterday to ask for them back. Since it was inconvenient in the temple, I invited him to the Jue Lu. The plaintiff then voluntarily wrote the IOU, it was not forced by me. Judge Luo understood that the monk's confession was completely false and immediately sentenced Dao Feng to two months in prison for attempted extortion, and confiscated the two IOUs.

A Youth in Western Clothing was Found Shot and Killed on Xizang Road Yesterday Morning

▲ A Note Found in His Pocket

▲ Seems to be a Warning to be Careful

▲ The Deceased Also Turns Out to be a Thug

▲ Cause of Assassination Not Yet Known

At half past two yesterday morning, a youth in Western clothing was found lying dead in Xiguiyang Lane on Xizang Road, his face covered in blood, and two shots in his leg. After a while, a rickshaw puller, Han Nangao, passed through the lane with a rubber-tired rickshaw. At first, he noticed a black shadow. Upon closer inspection, he saw that it was a person lying in a pool of blood. He was extremely frightened and shouted, running to report to the two Chinese policemen stationed at 1403 and 1450 Guangxi Road nearby. He led the two policemen back to the scene of the incident for inspection. The police reported to the Lao Zha Police Station by telephone, which dispatched Chinese and Western detectives by car to start an investigation. Unfortunately, it was late at night, and it was difficult to determine whether anyone had witnessed or heard anything. Then, a note was found in the deceased's pocket. Judging from the words in the note, it seemed that someone was aware that an assassination would be carried out and was telling him to escape quickly. However, the note was not signed, so it was impossible to know who wrote the note. The name of the deceased was also not written in the note, so it has not been found out yet. In addition to taking the note back to the police station, the detectives had the body transported to the forensic examination office on Feilun Road by car. After 10:00 a.m., the judge commissioned by the Provisional Court arrived at the office for inspection, ascended to the public seat, and according to the police chief, the deceased was found to be a thug who was involved in theft when he was alive. This killing may be a case of thugs killing each other or related to a theft case. However, it is still under investigation. Then, the rickshaw puller Chen Shuti recounted his discovery of the body and reported it to the police. The judge then ordered Pushan Villa to provide a guarantee and take the body away for burial.

Soldiers Hidden in a Pile of Bricks

▲ There is a Mauser Pistol in the Cement Pillar

▲ The Coal Shop Owner Seized the Opportunity to Escape

The Guanj Coal Shop at 837 Dongyouheng Road was found to be hiding military fire. The afternoon before yesterday, Yang A-quan, the detective chief of the Harbin Police Station, and detective Zhou Kai-wen drove to search it. They found a Mauser pistol and 112 bullets in a pile of bricks in the store. They also saw eight cement pillars in the patio, each about four feet long and five inches wide, which seemed suspicious. They used iron tools to break five of the pillars and did not find any contraband. The remaining three were not destroyed. These pillars were deposited by Yao Asheng, a former special agency detective. The police station reported that Yao had bullets stored in the pillars, so they destroyed them upon seeing them. However, the coal shop owner, Han Changmao from Jiangbei, had seized the opportunity to escape. Therefore, Li Changsheng, his watchman, was taken back to the police station along with the guns, bullets, and stone pillars. Later, Wang Sanzi, a person involved, was arrested on Disui Road. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Provisional Court. Han Changmao also surrendered to the court with his attorney Ye Fukang. Judge Xu conducted the trial. Wang Sanzi confessed that he used to be a driver at Yao Detective's house. In March of the previous year, a friend of Yao brought three Mauser pistols and placed them on the table. Yao and his friend were talking quietly, their voices low so that others could not hear them. Two weeks later, the friend came again and brought eight cement pillars. Yao ordered someone to make one more pillar like the others and ordered me to send them to the Guanj Coal Shop for deposit. Han was not in the store at the time, so he contacted Han's brother. Li Changsheng confessed that the shopkeeper ordered him to take out one of the nine stone pillars and break it the morning before, and he saw a wooden case for a Mauser pistol at one end and an iron box at the other end. He did not know what was in the box. When questioned, Han Changmao confessed that the stone pillars had been deposited for many years. The morning before, Li Changsheng wanted to move them, and one of the pillars broke, revealing a Mauser pistol and more than one hundred bullets. He was afraid and hid them in a pile of bricks. Attorney Ye also requested that Han be released on bail. Judge Xu ordered that Han be detained and that Wang and Li each pay a bail of 500 yuan and be interrogated again at a later date after the investigation is clear.

Capital to Build Large Wireless Radio Broadcasting Station

▲ Contract Signed with German Company

The Continental Daily reports that the National Government will build a large wireless radio broadcasting station in the capital, which will be as powerful and broadcast as widely as the largest broadcasting station in the world. The station will be constructed by the German Telefunken East Asia Wireless Telegraph Company. The Shanghai representative is Siemens Yangxing. The contract was signed on the 19th of this month by the Central Executive Committee and the German company. It stipulates that the station will use the latest Telefunken radio waves, which will not only cover the entire country, but also be heard in Europe. The broadcast transmitter plant will soon be built on the riverbank, with two steel columns, each 400 feet high, for installing antennas. The electricity will be generated by the plant itself, with a 600 horsepower engine. All automatic management and safety equipment will use the latest models. The broadcasting studio will be in the heart of the city, with a special cable to reach the transmitter plant. All government departments and bureaus, as well as theaters and entertainment venues, will be connected to the broadcasting studio. It is said that after the station is completed, it will be completely managed by Chinese people. Therefore, the National Government will send several radio engineers to Germany this week to investigate the organization and current situation of the German broadcasting industry in order to adopt it in the future.

The Problem of Separation and Reunion of a Couple of Ten Days

Han Wu, a woman from Anhui, is currently 58 years old and lives in Lujia Weir, Maogong Bridge, Longhua. She has one son and one daughter. The daughter, Wen Shu, also known as Mao Tou (now known as Ji Han), is currently 24 years old. After her husband died, she lived a hard life. In the Republic of China in 1928, Wen Shu married Ji Ke Gong (currently 25 years old), who lives in Xizhen, Old Longhua, as his wife at the behest of her parents and the words of the matchmaker. Ji is currently employed in the Transportation Corps First Regiment Wireless Communications First Team Headquarters of the Army, Navy and Air Force Headquarters. They married on October 29 of the same year. Before ten days had passed, he packed up and went to work in Hankou, Guangdong, and other places. He often wrote to his parents, expressing his unwillingness about this marriage and repeatedly wanting to break the marriage. He also wrote to his wife, willing to change his wife into a brother-sister relationship, advising his wife to marry someone else to avoid delaying her youth. However, Wen Shu was extremely stubborn, saying that once married, she would be married forever and that a woman would not marry twice. Ji Ke Gong has been away from home for several years and has not returned to Shanghai. Therefore, Wen Shu hired a lawyer yesterday to draft a complaint and filed it with the Shanghai Local Court, requesting that the court order them to live together as husband and wife and to order him to bear the cost of maintenance in order to maintain her livelihood.

Divorce Problems of an Elderly Couple

▲The final debate was announced yesterday

Mrs. Wu, the wife of Liu Dongsheng, a Suzhou native and owner of Quan Chang Zhu Diamond Store on Avenue Edward VII, is 57 years old. She claims that when she married Liu, he was only 21 years old and working as a shop assistant at Lao Jie Fu Silk Store in Shanghai with a monthly salary of two yuan. Therefore, she provided the dowry and instructed Liu to start a jewelry business. In a few years, they became moderately wealthy, but Liu suddenly forgot the wife who had seen him through hard times and took Tao as a concubine. Liu always favored and protected his concubine, making it impossible for Mrs. Wu to live at home. Last year, she hired a lawyer to sue Liu in the Provisional Court, requesting a maintenance fee of 30,000 yuan. Liu is now over sixty years old, and the white-haired couple frequently appeared in court. The judge, seeing that both parties were already old, suggested that they could grow old together and advised them to settle out of court. Unexpectedly, both old people were stubborn and unwilling to compromise, so mediation was difficult. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Feng Shide resumed the trial. Mrs. Wu first stated that the settlement had failed because the defendant was insincere. She then requested that the defendant be ordered to pay a one-time maintenance fee of 30,000 yuan or 80 yuan per month. The defendant claimed that the plaintiff had no intention of settling and that she had taken everything with her when she left home. Judge Feng still advised both parties to settle in court and provide some financial support to the plaintiff, but the defendant refused. He then summoned the witness Feng Yunhai for questioning. According to Feng, Liu did not share a room with the plaintiff, so the plaintiff had no choice but to leave. The witness also described in detail the ferocity of Liu's concubine, Tao. Then the debate began. After the lawyers for both sides finished their arguments, the court announced the end of the debate and scheduled a date for sentencing.

The Case of Liu Ling Beating His Apprentice to Death Concludes

▲The demand for compensation is enormous

▲The parties failed to reach a settlement

Tao Jupeng (15 years old), a martial arts apprentice learning from the actor Li Ruiting, was entrusted to his uncle Liu Fuchu (also known as Liu Yuchun) for instruction last winter when Li went to Suzhou to perform. However, Liu was violent and would beat him severely if he was not satisfied, causing internal injuries to Jupeng. He became seriously ill on October 15th last year, and Liu sent someone to take him to Yongchuan Hospital, but he died before he could be treated. After Jupeng's mother, Tao Cao, reported the incident to the police, the Provisional Court investigated. The details have been reported in the newspaper. Tao Cao then sued Li Ruiting and Liu Fuchu in the Provisional Court. Liu avoided appearing in court, and the presiding judge acquitted Li and issued a warrant for Liu Fuchu's arrest for further interrogation. Hou Fulin, a Chinese detective from the Xinzha Police Station, arrested Liu at the Xianshi Rooftop Garden and detained him. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Tan Xinzhen specially convened the First Court to resume the trial. The plaintiff's lawyer questioned the witness Li Tianbao. However, Li's testimony was inconsistent with his testimony at the autopsy. The plaintiff's lawyer stated to the court that Li's testimony was inconsistent and asked for attention. Dr. Wang Zhenchuan testified that the deceased had previously suffered from hemoptysis, which he had cured, and that his body was quite strong and had no diseases. However, when Tao was sent to his hospital, he was already dead. The autopsy revealed a blue mark about half an inch long on the deceased's leg and a similar injury on his lower abdomen. The cause of death was injury, but he could not prove what kind of injury was sustained. When questioned, Liu Fuchu denied beating Tao Jupeng to death. Judge Tan, seeing that the plaintiff Tao Cao's situation was quite pitiful, ordered Liu to provide some compensation. Liu claimed that he was poor and could not afford a large amount of compensation. However, the deceased's older sister, Tao Mengfei, claimed that Liu's family had a lot of property and that his mother specialized in lending money at high interest, earning thousands of yuan per month. Therefore, she demanded compensation of 24,000 yuan. The matter remained unresolved for a long time, but the settlement broke down due to the large difference in the amounts. After the lawyers for both sides finished their arguments, the court ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and scheduled a date for sentencing.

Girl Mistakenly Drinks Nitric Acid

▲Instant Death

Jin Xiuying, a 7-year-old girl, whose father is Faxiang, 29 years old, a Suzhou native, works as a dyer at Dahua Yarn Factory at No. 150, Alcock Road. At 7:40 PM the other day, Xiuying was playing at the Dahua Factory when she saw a cup of nitric acid. Thinking it was a tea drink, she picked it up and drank it. Shortly after, her father found out and sent Xiuying to the hospital, where she died instantly. The hospital reported it to the Huishan Police Station, which ordered detectives to send the body to the coroner's office. He ascended to the official position and, according to the report of the corpse's father, Jin Faxiang, stated: "The deceased child, Jin Xiuying, was verified to have died from mistakenly drinking nitric acid during her lifetime. The corpse will be handed over to her father, Jin Faxiang, to sign for burial."
